[APPENDIX ]A.—COPPER-PLATES, 1956-57



ANDHRA



ARIE/1956-1957/A/1956-57/1 (page )
Place
Dr. R.Subrahmanyam, Superintendent, Department of Archaeology, Guntur.
Dynasty
Vishṇukuṇḍin
King
Vikramēndrabhaṭṭārakavarṃan
Date
Regnal Year 14, grī. 2, pratipad.
Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit, Southern
Remarks
Registers a royal grant of the village Tūṇḍi, adjoining Va[ksha]pūru (?) to Svāmiśarman, son of Rudraśarman of Kauṇḍinya-gōtra and Āpastamba-sūtra and a resident of Āki. Gives the genealogy of the king for four generations, viz., Mādhavavarman, his son Vikramēndravarman, his son Indrabhaṭṭārakavarman and his son Vikramēndrabhaṭṭārakavarman.
ARIE/1956-1957/A/1956-57/2 (page )
Place
Photographs from Sri Seshadri Sastri, Guntur. Findspot: Vunna Guruvāya-pālem, Podili Taluk, Nellore District.
Dynasty
Pallava
King
Paramēśvaravarman I
Date
Year 19, Pausha śu. 13, Sunday, Uttarāyaṇa-saṅkrānti.
Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit, Southern
Remarks
Registers a grant of the village Kubuṇūru situated on the southern bank of the river Musuṇa in Pūmīrāshṭra by the king to Dēvaśarman, son of Dōṇaśarman and grandson of Svārriśarman of Maudgalya-gōtra and Āpastamba-charaṇa. The members of the donee's family are stated to have hailed from the village Ur-puṭūru-grāma. The executor of the grant was Kuḷa-varman, son of [Nāgi]-pallava and the ruler of Nanda-kuṟṟa. Published in Ep. Ind., Vol. XXXII, pp. 91 ff.
ARIE/1956-1957/A/1956-57/3 (page )
Place
Sri Manda Narasimham, Arasavalli, Srikakulam District.
Dynasty
Eastern Gaṅga
King
Rājēndravarman, son of Anantavarman
Date
Gaṅga year 313
Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit, Kaliṅga
Remarks
Registers grants of the village Pāṭṭali included in Kṛishṇa-maṭṭamba by Yuvarāja Rājēndravarman for the bali and other offerings to the goddess Kañchipoṭṭi-bhaṭṭārikā and of the villages Arali and Kuśasaṅkṅa-grāma by his mother Lōkamahādēvī, making the villages tax-free, for the merit of (her) parents and or her own merit. The charter was drafted by the Mahāsāndhivigrahika Sāmirāja and engraved by the akshaśāilin Dāmachandra. Published in Bhārati, Vol. XXXI, Part I, p. 574; Ep. Ind., Vol. XXXII, pp. 201 ff.
ARIE/1956-1957/A/1956-57/4 (page )
Place
Sri B.V.Krishna Rao, M.A., B.L., Danavayipeta, Rajahmundry.
Dynasty
Velama
King
Rājā Rao Janārdana Raṅgarāya
Date
Hēmalainbi, Kārttika śu. 15, Thursday, lunar eclipse.
Language & Alphabet
Telugu
Remarks
Registers a grant of land as agrahāra to Apparāyāchāryulu of Dōsapāḍu, Kṟishṇamma of Chilukūru and Kṛishṇamma of Mayilavaram in the name of Veṅkatṟā-yaniṅgāru by the chief. In late characters.

Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit, Telugu
Remarks
Stray plates containing portions of a list of the donees, with details of their gōtras etc. Some of the names are Prōlay-ādhyāpaka, Alāḍanāthārya, both of the Gārgya gōtra, Vaikuṇṭha-bhaṭṭa of Ātrēya-gōtra, Gaṅgādhara-bhaṭṭa, Annama-bhaṭṭa and Sōmaya-bhaṭṭa, all of the Śrīvatsa gōtra etc. In characters of the 13th century A.D. ARIE/1956-1957/A/1956-57/6 (page 26)
Place
Sri B.V. Krishna Rao, M.A., B.L., Danavayipeta, Rajahmundry.
Dynasty
…
King
…
Date
…
Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit, Telugu
Remarks
Stray plate containing portions of a record registering grant of the villages Oḍali and Chīluvūru as an agrahāra of 90 shares of which 5 were set apart for a deity and the rest distributed among the donees of whom some received one share, some half and the rest a quarter apiece, the exceptions among them being one who was a recipient of three shares, and two, of a share and a quarter each. The lists of the donees and the details of the donor and the date of the grant are all lost. See No. 5 above.

BOMBAY



ARIE/1956-1957/A/1956-57/18 (page 27)
Place
Director of Archives, Bombay. Thro-ugh Dr. D.C.Sircar. Findspot: Chinchani, Dahanu Taluk, Thana District.
Dynasty
Rāshṭrakūṭa
King
Indra III
Date
Śaka 848, Vyaya, Vaiśākha śu. 3, Monday = 926 A.D., April 17, f.d.t. ·03.
Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit, Northern
Remarks
Records that the chief Madhumati alias Sugatipa of the Tājika race and the ruler of Saṁyāna-maṇḍala under Indrarāja, endowed the village Kāṇāḍuka in the Kō-limahāra-vishaya together with half a dhura of land in Dēvīhara-grāma at the instance of Annamaiya, son of Nārāyaṇabhaṭṭa and a friend of the minister Puvvaiya for the repairs and upkeep of the Maṭhikā constructed by Annamaiya for the offering of bhōga to the goddess Daśamī (therein ?), and for feeding nine Brāhmaṇas of the Pañcha-Gauḍīya-Mahāparishad settled at Sain-yāna. The creation of the endowment was declared by the chief at an assemblage of the Hamyamana-Pauras, Dhruvas and Vishayik-ādhikaraikas. Pub-lished in Ep. Ind., Vol. XXXII, pp. 45 ff.
ARIE/1956-1957/A/1956-57/19 (page 27)
Place
Do.
Dynasty
Do.
King
Kṛishṇa III
Date
…
Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit, Northern
Remarks
Records a vyavasthā by the deity Bhillamāladēva and His vārikas in the maṭhikā of the goddess stipulating payment of 40 drammas annually on the occasion of e dipōtsava-bhaṅga, by the svādhyāyikas of the Mahāparishad towards a piece of land that belonged to god Bhillamāladēva but was enclosed within the com-pound of the maṭhikā. Published in Ep. Ind., Vol. XXXII, pp. 55 ff.
ARIE/1956-1957/A/1956-57/20 (page 28)
Place
Director of Archives, Bombay. Thro-ugh Dr. D.C.Sircar. Findspot: Chinchani, Dahanu Taluk, Thana District.
Dynasty
Śilāhāra
King
Chhinturāja
Date
Śaka 956, Bhāva, Bhādrapada ba. 15.
Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit, Nāgarī
Remarks
Registers a gift of a ghāṇaka (oil-mill) by Mahāmaṇḍalē-śvara Chāmuṇḍarāja in favour of the Kautuka-maṭhikā at Samyāna for burning a lamp in front of the Bhagavatī and for besmearing oil on the feet of the svādhyāyikas (scholars) one of whom, Chhīhaḍa by name, received the gift which was made free from all obligations. The charter was written by Dhruva Mammalaiya. Published in Ep. Ind., Vol. XXXII, pp. 63 ff.
ARIE/1956-1957/A/1956-57/21 (page 28)
Place
Do.
Dynasty
Mōḍha
King
Vijjala
Date
Śaka 969, Māgha-saṅkrānti.
Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit, Nāgarī
Remarks
Records the grant of the siriḍirkā (tax ?) of the village Kāṇāḍḍa-grāma belonging to the Kavatika-mathikā in favour of the house-holders Bahudhara and Kāṅkua and the scholars Mahādēva and Lakshmīdhara by the chief after having worshipped god Mayūkhamālin and in consultation with his ministers Sarvādhikāra-niyukta-varishṭhaka Mummuraka and Thakkura Dōm-balaiya. Ibid. pp. 68 ff.
ARIE/1956-1957/A/1956-57/22 (page 28)
Place
Do.
Dynasty
Do.
King
Do.
Date
Śaka 975, Vijaya, Kārttika ba. 15, Solar eclipse = 1053 A.D., No-vember 13.
Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit, Nāgarī
Remarks
Registers the grant of three drammas received as siriḍikā on the village Kēṇasā-grāma belonging to the Kautuka-mathikā in favour of the householders and scholars attached to the maṭhikā as a permanent endowment for feeding 25 Brāhmaṇas by the chief, here called Mahāmaṇḍalēśvara Vijja-rāṇaka and stated to have been ruling over Sainyāna-pattana-700 which was a maṇḍala comprising 4000 draṅgas and extending as far as Ākāśikā. Mentions Varishṭhaka Mummuraka as the administrator of the kingdom and Mahā-ṭhakkura Dōmbalaiya as the administrator of Sainyāna (town). Ibid., pp. 71 ff.

ARIE/1956-1957/A/1956-57/24 (page 28)

Dr. Motichandra, Director, Prince of Wales Museum, Bombay. Find-spot: Thānā.

ARIE/1956-1957/A/1956-57/25 (page 29)
Place
Director, Indian Historical Research Institute, St. Xaviers College, Bombay. Through Dr. D.C. Sircar. Findspot: Bannahaḷḷi.

ARIE/1956-1957/A/1956-57/26 (page 29)
Place
Do.
Dynasty
Kadamba of Goa
King
Gūhalladēva
Date
Śaka 960, Bahudhā-nya, Chaitra śu. 15, Thursday, Lunar eclipse = 1038 A.D., March 23.
Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit, Nāgarī
Remarks
Registers a tax-free gift of the village Sāuvai-pāṭaka situated on the south-east corner of Dhēraka, by the king after having worshipped Lord Gōkarṇa on the shore of the sea, to Nārāyaṇa, the priest of the king and the brother of Gōvardhana, whose grandfather Mārēya-bhaṭṭa of the Sādyāyana gōtra is said to have migrated from Ambaramaṅgala in Kāchītitāsa-vishaya, to Chandra-pura. Text (faulty) published in Kadamba kula, pp. 387 ff.
ARIE/1956-1957/A/1956-57/27 (page 29)
Place
Do.
Dynasty
Vijayanagara
King
Immaḍi-Prauḍhadēvarāya
Date
Śaka 1378, (Vasu-adri-guṇa-bhū) Dhātri, Kārttika śu. 12, Sunday-1456 A.D., October 10, f.d.t. 87. The month was adhika.
Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit & Kannaḍa, Nandiḍ-nāgarī
Remarks
Registers the grant of the village O1ndūru in the Handi-khaṇḍa subdivision of Honnāvara-mahārājya to Śa-ṅkarārya, son of Basavaṇa of the Viśvāmitra gōtra, well-versed in the Ṛig-vēda, for offerings to God Mahābalē-śvara in the vicinity of Gōkarṇatīrtha, at the time of Rudrābhishēka and for expenses towards employing hands for cooking, conducting religious rites etc. The grant was made by the king at the instance of Ammappa-nāyaka, son of Khaḍaya Chennappa-nāyaka. The king is also referred to as Mallikārjuna earlīer in the charter. Vīraṇa, son of Muddaṇāchārya, was the engraver (lēkhaka) of the charter.
ARIE/1956-1957/A/1956-57/28 (page 29)
Place
Do.
Dynasty
…
King
…
Date
…
Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit, Mixed characters
Remarks
The language is very corrupt. The purport of the record is not clear. Mentions Puṇḍravardhana, a certain Jayakēśi-rāja and seems to eulogise some Brāhmaṇas well-versed in Jyōtiś-śāstra etc. The characters used are Nāgarī, Grantha and Telugu mixed up pell-mell. Contains a legend reading Śrī-Jayakēśi-suta-Mādhavadāsa enclosed within a circle at the end of the record.

RAJASTHAN



ARIE/1956-1957/A/1956-57/77 (page 35)

Chāhamānas of Nāḍōl
King
Āsārāja (?)
Date
…
Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit, Nāgarī
Remarks
Incomplete. Records the excavation of a tank in the fortress of Māṇḍavya (Maṇḍōr) by the king. Also records that Āsārāja killed the Turushkas (Muham-madans) when Pṛithvīpāla, his brother, was besieged by them. See An. Rep. Rajputana Museum, March 1937, p. 3, No. VII.
ARIE/1956-1957/A/1956-57/78 (page 35)
Place
Do. Stray Plate Findspot: Do.
Dynasty
Do.
King
…
Date
(1) V.S. 1171, Pausha ba. 10. (2) V.S. 1173, Kārttika ba. 3. (3) V.S. 1192, Kārttika ba. 5, Saturday. 1135 A.D. Septem-ber 28. (4) V.S. 1205, Bhādra ba. 5. Friday, = 1148 A.D. August 6
Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit, Nāgarī
Remarks
Records several grants (one being that of the village Bhiṇ-ṭalavāḍā) to Chandalēśvara and Tripurushadēva. Also records that Mahārājādhirāja Āsārāja, Mahārājādhirāja Ratnapāla and Mahārājaputra Sāhanapāla made some grants on different dates. I is also recorded that Mahā-rāja Ālhaṇadēva granted three kuṭumbins, called Kīkāu, Madanapāla and Mahaṇasīha Tripurushadēva. Ibid., No. VI. Published in Ep. Ind., Vol. XXXIII, pp. 238. ff.


RAJASTHAN



ARIE/1956-1957/A/1956-57/79 (page 36)
Place
Ajmer.—Rajputana Museum. Pho-tographs from the Curator. Findspot: Nānānā, Bhagawānpurā
Dynasty
Chaulukya
King
Kumārapāla
Date
(1) V.S. [12]19, Pau-shaba 3, Monday = 1162 A.D., Novem-ber 26. (2) V.S. 1220, Āshāḍha śu. 11, Thursday = 1164 A.D., July 2.
Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit, Nāgarī
Remarks
Written in two different hands. The first part records that Ālhaṇa, a feudatory of the king, restored the village of Nāndāṇā to the temple of Tripurushadeva in Saṁvat [12]19. The second part written in bolder characters registers that Ālhaṇa gave Bhītalavāṭaka (Bhintalavāṭaka ?) to the temple of Chandalēśvara and also four drammas per month to the temple of Gaurī built by his wife Śaṅkarādēvī inside the temple of Chandalēśvara. The writer of the first part is Khēlāditya. The second part also registers that Mahārājādhirāja Ālhaṇadēva granted some land in the village of Chāṁvōḍi to the temple of Tripurushadēva. The writer of this portion is Śrīdhara. Reported in the An. Rep. Rajputana Museum, p. 4, No. IX. March, 37, No. 4 B of 1914-15.

UTTAR PRADESH



ARIE/1956-1957/A/1956-57/81 (page 36)
Place
Curator, Bharat Kala Bhavan, Bana-ras.
Dynasty
Pratināra
King
Harirāja
Date
V.S. 1040, solar eclipse. Probably = 984 A.D., July 30.
Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit, Nāgarī
Remarks
Registers a grant of two hala of land in Tauḍā (or Katauḍā) grāma and ten house-sites in Tithāsēvaṇī grāma by the king while he was camping at Sīyaḍōṇī. The grant was made on the occasion of a solar eclipse and the reci-pient of the grant was the Brāhmaṇa Dēda, son of Śānti and grandson of Dharma of the Bhāradvāja gōtra, the three pravaras and the Vājasanēya sākhā. Published in Ep. Ind., Vol. XXXI pp. 309 ff.

FOREIGN COUNTRIES



CEYLON



ARIE/1956-1957/A/1956-57/85 (page 37)
Place
Ceylon.—Impression and photo-graphs of a copper-plate from the Archaeological Commissioner.
Dynasty
…
King
…
Date
Śaka 1537, Jaya, Tai 26, Friday. Irregu-lar.
Language & Alphabet
Tamil
Remarks
Seems to state that twelve Cheṭṭippiḷḷaimār of Madirai (Madura) brought the image of Chintadiraippiḷḷaiyār and installed it near (the image of) Kumāratti for which act they were granted some land in Maṭṭukkaḷappu Vīramuṉai on a representation made to the king of Ceylon who further ordered a levy of half a paṇam per head per annum on all the women of Maṭṭukkaḷappu-nāḍu to be paid to the piḷḷaimār in addition to granting them the siṁhamudrā, tirumukha and tirukkai.

WEST GODAVARI DISTRICT



NARASAPUR TALUK



ARIE/1956-1957/B/1956-57/8 (page 39)
Place
Narasāpur.—Madanagōpālasvāmin temple. Pillar set up outside the temple.
Dynasty
Eastern Chālukya (?)
King
Sarvalōkāśraya Vishṇuvardhana-mahārāja alias Vīrabhadrēśvara-dēvachakravartin.
Date
Year 15, Uttarāyaṇa-saṅkrānti.
Language & Alphabet
Telugu
Remarks
Registers a gift of the perpetual lamp to the temple of Mārkaṇḍīśvara and 55 buffaloes for the supply of ghee for burning the lamp by Pōtā-sāni, daughter of Māvena. The buffaloes were entrusted into the hands of Kētanabōya, son of Tātana-pāga stipulating that he should supply one sāniyamāna or sāniyamānika of ghee daily to the temple.
ARIE/1956-1957/B/1956-57/9 (page 39)
Place
Do. Same pillar.
Dynasty
Do.
King
Sarvalōkāśraya Vishṇuvardhana-ma-hārāja.
Date
Year [2]4, Chaitra śu. 13, Thursday, Vishu-va-saṅkrānti. Pro-bably = 1159 A.D., April 2. The saṅkrānti occurred on March 24.
Language & Alphabet
Telugu
Remarks
Records a gift of 50 buffaloes for the supply of one māna, (or mānika) of ghee daily for burning a perpetual lamp in the temple of Mārkaṇḍēśvara by Sūri-seṭṭi, son of Nāgi-seṭṭi of Jananāthapura. The buffaloes were en-trusted into the hands of Rēya-bōya, son of Yeṟiya-bōya. Records in addition a gift of 1 puṭṭi of land, probably by the same donor. See No. 11 below.

Do.—Slab in the O1nkārayya temple to the west of the village.
Dynasty
Chālukya of Ka-lyāṇa.
King
Bhūlōkamalla
Date
Year 12, Piṅgaḷa, Bhādrapada (wrong for Kārttika) amāvāsyā, Solar eclipse-1137 A.D., November 15.
Language & Alphabet
Kannaḍa
Remarks
Registers a gift of the village Bāḍambeyyaṁgēri in Tumbaḷu-30 as sarvanamasya to god Narasiṁhadēva (?) of Tum-baḷabīḍu Sindavāḍi-paṭṭaṇa by Mahāpradhāna Sēnādhipati Kaḍita-verggaḍe, Kannaḍa-sandhivigrahi, Hiriyadaṇḍanāyaka Kāḍimayya for expenses towards the repairs and upkeep of the temple, worship and offerings, perpetual lamps, feeding of the parichāra-Brāhmaṇas etc., in the temple. The gift was en-trusted into the hands of Īśvaraprakāśa-Bhaṭṭāraka. A third portion of the gift-village was made over to the heggaḍes of the temple headed by Kṛishṇa-bhaṭṭa.

Registers the document (Iraṇakkrayapramāṇa-iśaivu-tīṭṭu) given by Maṇkoṇḍāṉ Dēvāṇḍāṉ of Ālattūr recording the sale of his land at Nelvayal alias Kulōttuṅgaśōlanallūr in Aḷa-nāḍu in lieu of 510 kalañju of gold which he owed to the tāṉattār. ARIE/1956-1957/B/1956-57/322 (page 76)
Place
Do. Eastern parapet on the left side wall.
Dynasty
Guhila
King
Kumbhakarṇa
Date
V.S. 1507, Śrāvaṇa śu. 11, Sunday = 1451 A.D., August 8.
Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit, Nāgarī
Remarks
States that the work was caused to be done by the king through the architect Ji(Ja)ītā.
ARIE/1956-1957/B/1956-57/323 (page 76)
Place

Do.

Sanskrit, Nāgarī
Remarks

ARIE/1956-1957/B/1956-57/335 (page 77)
Place
Do. Western wall to the left
Dynasty
Guhila
King
Kuṁbhakarṇa
Date
V.S. 15109 (for 1509 ?), Śrāvaṇa śu. 11, Monday = 1453 A.D., July 16.
Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit, Nāgarī
Remarks
Refers to the construction of the Kīrttistaṁbha of Rāṇā Kuṁbhakarṇa, the masons Nāpā, Bhūmī and Bhuthī, who were the sons of Jaītā. cf. Bhandarkar's List, No. 313.

ARIE/1956-1957/B/1956-57/456 (page 83)
Place
Do. Eighth floor. Stone slab in a niche in the north-east corner.
Dynasty
[Guhila]
King
[Kumbhakarṇa]
Date
…
Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit, Nāgarī
Remarks
Contains the beginning (verses 1-28) of a praśasti apparently of Rāṇā Kuṁbhakarṇa in 32 lines. Mentions Bappa (l. 4), Hammīra (ll. 11-12), Raghu-bhūpa (l. 21), Chēlavāṭa (l. 22), Kshētrasiṁha and Chitrakūṭa (l. 25) and Raṇamalla (l. 27). See Cun-ningham, ASI., Vol. XXIII, pp. 111-12 and plates XX-XXI; and PRAS., WC., 1903-04, p. 56, Nos. 2053-54 and Bhandarka's List, No. 797.
ARIE/1956-1957/B/1956-57/457 (page 84)
Place
Tower of Fame. Stone slab in a niche in the north-west corner.
Dynasty
Guhila
King
Kuṁbhakarṇa
Date
(1) V.S. 1507, Kā-rttika, first fortnight 13; (2) V.S. 1515, Chaitra ba. 13; (3) V.S. 1505, Māgha śu. 10; (4) V.S. 1509 (Nanḍa-vyōma-ishu-śītadyuti), Māgha pūrṇā, i.e. 5, 10 or 15.
Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit, Nāgarī
Remarks
Contains a portion, (verses 169-187) apparently of the praśasti mentioned above in 26 lines. Refers to Kuṁbha-karṇa's resistance against the combined forces of the Gūrjara and Mālava kings and Suratrāṇa or Sult6ān (ll. 1-6); some vague victory of his over the Yavanas or the Muhammadans (ll. 7-8); his three officers who were in charge of horses, elephants and soldiers respectively, subordinate to Tōḍaramalla (l. 11); his part as Ādivarāha in lifting the earth from the ocean that was the Turushka army (l. 12); his father Śrī-Mōkala and mother Saubhāgya-dēvī (ll. 13-14) as well as wife Kuṁbhalladēvī (l. 16); his construc-tion of a new viśikhā (street) on Śrī-Chitrakūṭa (ll. 19-20); his building of Śrī-Kuṁbhamēru (ll. 21-22); his erection of the Kīrttistaṁbha or the Tower of Fame on the mountain of Śrī-Chitrakūṭa (ll. 22-23) and lastly, his completion of the fortification of the fort. See Bhandarkar's List, No. 797.

ARIE/1956-1957/B/1956-57/203 (page 107)
Place
Temple No. 28. Inscription No. 1. (Pedestal of an image)
Dynasty
…
King
…
Date
…
Language & Alphabet
Sanskrit, Nāgarī
Remarks
Seems to contain two records of which the first one states that Rāmachaṁdra-paṇḍita with the help of the Chatur-vidha-saṁgha, made the image. The second one seems to mention the name of Mādhavachaṁdra, disciple of Sahasraki(kīrtti)-paṁḍita. There are engraved two calves (=) facing one tree in the middle. Probably the calves represent the bull, the emblem of Ādīnātha and the tree the banyan tree. (Symbol—deer and wheel).
